            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palomares, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Serras, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Villaluenga, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hueso, K. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carretero-González, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5884</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5901</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c2ee02781j</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00643K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, S. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, B. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K. Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An open-framework iron fluoride and reduced graphene oxide nanocomposite as a high-capacity cathode material for Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of high-rate cathodes particularly with remarkable wide-temp.-tolerance sodium-storage capability plays a significant role in com. applications of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, we devise a scaled-up electrospinning avenue to fabricate nanocrystal-constructed ultralong layered NaCrO2 nanowires (NWs) toward SIBs as a wide-temp.-operating cathode.  The resultant one-dimensional (1D) NaCrO2 nanoarchitecture is endowed with orientated and shortened electronic/ionic transport and remarkable structural tolerance to stress change over sodiation-desodiation processes. Promisingly, the NaCrO2 NWs exhibit extraordinary high-rate capacities of ∼108.8 and ∼87.2 mAh g-1 at 10 and 50 C rates at 25°, and even 94.6 (55°) and ∼60.1 (-15°) mAh g-1 at 10 C, along with outstanding cyclic stabilities with capacity retentions of ∼80.6% (-15°), 88.4% (25°), and ∼86.9% (55°). Encouragingly, a competitive energy d. of ∼161 Wh kg-1 can be obtained by the NaCrO2 NWs-based full cell.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering the abundant sodium resources, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) demonstrate great potential in large-scale electrochem. energy storage sectors which capacity and cycle stability is highly dependent on their electrode materials.  Layered P2-type Mn-Fe-based oxide has been considered as one of the most promising cathodes for SIBs, while its unsatisfactory cycle performance and low energy d. strongly limit practical application.  Here, a Co/Ni modification strategy is proposed to optimize P2-Na2/3Mn1/2Fe1/2O2 (MF) from both aspects of reversible capacity and cycle stability, leading to the design of a new P2-Na2/3Mn1/2Fe1/4Co1/8Ni1/8O2 (MFCN).  In this new layered P2-type material, the introduction of Co effectively inhibits the irreversibility of the material, and the introduction of Ni relieves the Jahn-Teller effect and reduces Mn dissoln.  The simultaneous introduction of Co and Ni effectively improves the cycle stability of the electrode, indicated by the increase of the capacity retention rate from 51.5% for MF to 87.4% for MFCN over 100 discharge-charge cycles at the same c.d. of 130 mA g-1.  Meanwhile, the introduction of Ni effectively increases the discharge voltage with the middle discharge voltage increasing from 2.8 V (MF) to 3.3 V (MFCN), thereby improving the energy d. of the electrode.  All above features make the new material highly promising for use as a cathode material in practical SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2018.11.214"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The novel P3-type layered Na<sub>0.65</sub>Mn<sub>0.75</sub>Ni<sub>0.25</sub>O<sub>2</sub> oxides doped by non-metallic elements for high performance sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na layered oxides NaxCoO2 form one of the most fascinating low-dimensional and strongly correlated systems; in particular P2-NaxCoO2 exhibits various single-phase domains with different Na+/vacancy patterns depending on the Na concn.  Here the authors used Na batteries to clearly depict the P2-NaxCoO2 phase diagram for x ≥ 0.50.  By coupling the electrochem. process with an in situ x-ray diffraction expt., the authors identified the succession of single-phase or two-phase domains appearing on Na intercalation with a rather good accuracy compared with previous studies.  The authors reported new single-phase domains and the authors underlined the thermal instability of some ordered phases from an electrochem. study at various temps.  As each phase was characterized by the position of its Fermi level vs. the Na+/Na couple, the synthesis of each material, even in large amts., can be carried out electrochem.  The phys. properties of the as-prepd. Na1/2CoO2 and Na2/3CoO2 ordered phases were characterized and compared.  Electrochem. processes are an accurate route to precisely study in a continuous way such a complex system and provide a new way to synthesize materials with a very narrow existence range.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1021/cm101377h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moreau, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guyomard, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gaubicher, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Boucher, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure and Stability of Sodium Intercalated Phases in Olivine FePO<sub>4</sub></span>. <i>Chem. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1201</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tracking lithium transport and electrochemical reactions in nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Feng; Yu Hui-Chia; Chen Min-Hua; Wu Lijun; Pereira Nathalie; Thornton Katsuyo; Van der Ven Anton; Zhu Yimei; Amatucci Glenn G; Graetz Jason</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1201</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Expectations for the next generation of lithium batteries include greater energy and power densities along with a substantial increase in both calendar and cycle life.  Developing new materials to meet these goals requires a better understanding of how electrodes function by tracking physical and chemical changes of active components in a working electrode.  Here we develop a new, simple in-situ electrochemical cell for the transmission electron microscope and use it to track lithium transport and conversion in FeF(2) nanoparticles by nanoscale imaging, diffraction and spectroscopy.  In this system, lithium conversion is initiated at the surface, sweeping rapidly across the FeF(2) particles, followed by a gradual phase transformation in the bulk, resulting in 1-3 nm iron crystallites mixed with amorphous LiF.  The real-time imaging reveals a surprisingly fast conversion process in individual particles (complete in a few minutes), with a morphological evolution resembling spinodal decomposition.  This work provides new insights into the inter- and intra-particle lithium transport and kinetics of lithium conversion reactions, and may help to pave the way to develop high-energy conversion electrodes for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201002879"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A strategy for enabling highly insulated FeF3 as high performance cathode materials for NIBs is proposed and realized, through constructing metallic Fe and reduced graphene oxide (RGO) double enhancement conducting matrix, wherein both the metallic Fe and active FeF3 are in situ electrochem. generated from one FeF2 grain (as precursor of FeF3) to ensure their desired homogenous and intimate contact. The major bottleneck should be lack of any effective engineering techniques to make reliable encapsulation and conducting matrix on sol. FeFx species. Therefore, both structures need to be controlled.  A comparative state-of-the-art review of catalysts and supports is provided along with detailed synthesis methods.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A fluoride-based cathode (FeF3·0.33H2O) for lithium batteries, the synthesis of which has been reported recently, is described in terms of structure, morphol., and performance.  A self-assembled mesoporous morphol. connected with a high sp. surface area is obtained through the soft template role of the ionic liq.  The fluoride exhibits a one-dimensional tunnel structure produced by continuous hexagonal cavities, in which hydration water mols. are located.  The high Li-intercalation activity of carbon-free FeF3·0.33H2O is expected to be assocd. with various factors, including electrolyte-infiltratable mesoporosity, wide Li+-insertable channels, and medium conductivities.  A single solid-soln. reaction mechanism is indicated by potentiostatic intermittent titrn. technique and ex situ X-ray diffraction at different reactive potentials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.6b00061"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jacobs, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morgan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Origins of Large Voltage Hysteresis in High-Energy-Density Metal Fluoride Lithium-Ion Battery Conversion Electrodes</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>138</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2838</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2848</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.6b00061</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origins of Large Voltage Hysteresis in High-Energy-Density Metal Fluoride Lithium-Ion Battery Conversion Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Linsen; Jacobs, Ryan; Gao, Peng; Gan, Liyang; Wang, Feng; Morgan, Dane; Jin, Song</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2838-2848</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal fluorides and oxides can store multiple lithium ions through conversion chem. to enable high-energy-d. lithium-ion batteries.  However, their practical applications have been hindered by an unusually large voltage hysteresis between charge and discharge voltage profiles and the consequent low-energy efficiency (&lt;80%).  The phys. origins of such hysteresis are rarely studied and poorly understood.  Here we employ in situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy, transmission electron microscopy, d. functional theory calcns., and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique to first correlate the voltage profile of iron fluoride (FeF3), a representative conversion electrode material, with evolution and spatial distribution of intermediate phases in the electrode.  The results reveal that, contrary to conventional belief, the phase evolution in the electrode is sym. during discharge and charge.  However, the spatial evolution of the electrochem. active phases, which is controlled by reaction kinetics, is different.  We further propose that the voltage hysteresis in the FeF3 electrode is kinetic in nature.  It is the result of ohmic voltage drop, reaction overpotential, and different spatial distributions of electrochem. active phases (i.e., compositional inhomogeneity).  Therefore, the large hysteresis can be expected to be mitigated by rational design and optimization of material microstructure and electrode architecture to improve the energy efficiency of lithium-ion batteries based on conversion chem.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.01.080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, B. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahn, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, S. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K. Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Probing the Sodiation-Desodiation Reactions in Nano-sized Iron Fluoride Cathode</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>191</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">307</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">316</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2016.01.080</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Probing the Sodiation-Desodiation Reactions in Nano-sized Iron Fluoride Cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ali, Ghulam; Lee, Ji-Hoon; Cho, Byung Won; Nam, Kyung-Wan; Ahn, Docheon; Chang, Wonyoung; Oh, Si Hyoung; Chung, Kyung Yoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">191</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">307-316</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A hybrid nanocomposite of FeF3·0.5H2O and MWCNTs was synthesized as a high-performance cathode material for room-temp. Na-ion batteries.  The composite exhibits remarkably high capacity (197 mAh g-1) and stable cycle performance (148 mAh g-1 at the 100th cycle with a 0.05 C rate) accompanying with the unique nanostructure of the material and the incorporation of MWCNTs.  The addn. of MWCNTs not only increases the cond. of the active material but also plays a role to design a unique morphol. where nano-sized FeF3·0.5H2O particles are grown both inside and outside of the MWCNTs.  The Na diffusion coeff. of the composite material is detd. by galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique during dis/charging and the values are at 10-12-10-14 cm2 s-1 which are lesser than Li diffusion coeff. of FeF3 (10-10-10-12 cm2 s-1).  In situ x-ray diffraction coupled with ex situ high resoln. TEM is employed to study the phase transition behavior.  The results reveal both cryst. and amorphous phases upon Na insertion.  Also, ex situ NEXAFS spectroscopy (at the F K-edge and Fe L3-edge) is conducted at different potential steps to det. the change in oxidn. state and local structure.  NEXAFS spectra reveal the conversion reaction mechanism and reversibility of the material as evidenced by the de/formation of NaF during de/sodiation process.  The combined study of in situ XRD and NEXAFS will give valuable information on de/sodiation reactions in FeF3·0.5H2O.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1016/j.est.2018.04.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hollow porous FeF<sub>3</sub> ·0.33H <sub>2</sub>O microspheres by AlPO<sub>4</sub> coating as a cathode material of Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Journal of Energy Storage.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>18</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">103</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">111</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.est.2018.04.026</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1021/ja402061q"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dinnebier, R. E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An FeF<sub>(3)</sub>.0.5H<sub>2</sub>O polytype: a microporous framework compound with intersecting tunnels for Li and Na batteries</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>135</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">11425</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11428</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja402061q</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An FeF3·0.5H2O Polytype: A Microporous Framework Compound with Intersecting Tunnels for Li and Na Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Chilin; Yin, Congling; Gu, Lin; Dinnebier, Robert E.; Mu, Xiaoke; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">135</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">31</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11425-11428</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the energy/power d. of energy storage materials, numerous efforts have focused on the exploration of new structure prototypes, in particular metal-org. fameworks, Prussian blue analogs, open-framework oxides, and polyanion salts.  Here the authors report a novel pyrochlore phase that appears to be useful as a high-capacity cathode for Li and Na batteries.  It is an Fe fluoride polymorph characterized by an intersecting tunnel structure, providing the space for accommodation and transport of Li and Na ions.  It is prepd. using hydrolyzable ionic liqs., which serve as reaction educts and structure-directing agents not only as far as the chem. structure is concerned but also in terms of morphol. (shape, defect structure, electrode network structure).  A capacity &gt;220 mA h g-1 (for Li and Na storage) and a lifetime of ≥300 cycles (for Li storage) are demonstrated.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1021/ja902639w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamakawa, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Key, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Grey, C. P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Identifying the Local Structures Formed during Lithiation of the Conversion Material, Iron Fluoride, in a Li Ion Battery: A Solid-State NMR, X-ray Diffraction, and Pair Distribution Function Analysis Study</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2009</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>131</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">10525</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">10536</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja902639w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Identifying the Local Structures Formed during Lithiation of the Conversion Material, Iron Fluoride, in a Li Ion Battery: A Solid-State NMR, X-ray Diffraction, and Pair Distribution Function Analysis Study</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yamakawa, Naoko; Jiang, Meng; Key, Baris; Grey, Clare P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">131</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">30</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10525-10536</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The structural transformations that occur when FeF3 is cycled at room temp. in a Li cell were investigated using a combination of x-ray diffraction (XRD), pair distribution function (PDF) anal., and magic-angle-spinning NMR spectroscopy.  Two regions are seen on discharge.  The first occurs between Li = 0 and 1.0 and involves an insertion reaction.  This first region actually comprises two steps.  First, a two-phase reaction between Li = 0 and 0.5 occurs, and the Li0.5FeF3 phase that is formed gives rise to a Li NMR resonance due to Li+ ions near both Fe3+ and Fe2+ ions.  On the basis of the PDF data, the local structure of this phase is closer to the rutile structure than the original ReO3 structure.  Second, a single-phase intercalation reaction occurs between Li = 0.5 and 1.0, for which the Li NMR data indicate a progressive increase in the concn. of Fe2+ ions.  In the second region, the conversion reaction, superparamagnetic, nanosized (∼3 nm) Fe metal is formed, as indicated by the XRD and NMR data, along with some LiF and a third phase that is rich in Li and F.  The charge process involves the formation of a series of intercalation phases with increasing Fe oxidn. state, which, on the basis of the Li NMR and PDF data, have local structures that are similar to the intercalation phases seen during the first stage of the discharge process.  The solid-state NMR and XRD results for the rutile phase FeF2 are presented for comparison, and the data indicate that an insertion reaction also occurs, which is accompanied by the formation of LiF.  This is followed by the formation of Fe nanoparticles and LiF via a conversion reaction.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1002/sia.740100203"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hawn, D. D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">DeKoven, B. M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Deconvalution as a Correction for Photoelectron Inelastic Energy Losses in the Core Level XPS Spectra of Iron Oxides</span>. <i>Surf. Interface Anal.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1987</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">63</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">74</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/sia.740100203</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Deconvolution as a correction for photoelectron inelastic energy losses in the core level XPS spectra of iron oxides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hawn, David D.; DeKoven, Benjamin M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Surface and Interface Analysis</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1987</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2-3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">63-74</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SIANDQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0142-2421</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Core level XPS spectra of polycryst. Fe metal and several oxides are cor. by deconvolution using the ratio method for energy loss effects and spectral broadening due to both an achromatic x-ray source and finite analyzer resoln.  These ideas are applied to the XPS spectra of Fe, FeO, Fe2O3, and Fe3O4 to obtain the intrinsic lineshape.  The backscattered electron energy loss spectra are effective in distinguishing Fe and its oxides.  For Fe metal and its oxides, the electron energy loss deconvolved spectra have a flat baseline and enhanced resoln.  This background removal method is more reliable than either linear or sigmoidal background approxns.  This allows for a detn. of the relative sensitivity factor for the Fe 2p and O 1s core levels.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i12">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.0c01652?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.0c01652</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Detailed calculation process of TG, N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption isotherms, and the BJH pore size distribution of FeF<sub>3</sub>·0.33H<sub>2</sub>O NPs (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.0c01652/suppl_file/am0c01652_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.0c01652/suppl_file/am0c01652_si_001.pdf">am0c01652_si_001.pdf (540.09 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="93187ff4cb7c075b-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

// Moving the popup before the header content for tab accessibility
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => {
    const headerNode = $('.header_content');
    const popupNode = $('.pairing-affiliations-popup');

        <!-- <h2>System Message</h2> -->
        <span class="system-message-date">Thursday, April 17, 2025</span>
        <p>Please be aware that pubs.acs.org is undergoing maintenance from Saturday February 1 to Monday Febraury 3, that may have an impact on your experience. During this time, you may not be able to access certain features like login, purchasing single articles, saving searches or running existing saved searches, modifying your e-Alert preferences, or accessing Librarian administrative functions. <script nonce="93187ff4cb7c075b-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();

          //   console.log(event.target);

        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");

          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>

        <script nonce="93187ff4cb7c075b-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){

                    cookie=status;

            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
